      <p><b>Ecuador</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Ecuador.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/89/En-us-Ecuador.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Ecuador.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">EK</span>-wə-dor</i></a>; <small>Spanish pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[ekwaˈðoɾ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:ES-pe_-_Ecuador.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/ES-pe_-_Ecuador.ogg" class="internal" title="ES-pe - Ecuador.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <a href="/wiki/Quechuan_languages" title="Quechuan languages">Quechua</a>: <i>Ikwayur</i>; <a href="/wiki/Shuar_language" title="Shuar language">Shuar</a>: <i>Ecuador</i> or <i>Ekuatur</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Ecuador</b> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">República del Ecuador</i>, which literally translates as "Republic of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>"; <a href="/wiki/Quechuan_languages" title="Quechuan languages">Quechua</a>: <i>Ikwadur Ripuwlika</i>; <a href="/wiki/Shuar_language" title="Shuar language">Shuar</a>: <i>Ekuatur Nunka</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in northwestern <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, bordered by <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> on the north, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> on the east and south, and the Pacific Ocean on the west. Ecuador also includes the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a> in the Pacific, about 1,000 kilometres (621&nbsp;mi) west of the mainland. The capital is <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Proyecciones_Poblacionales_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proyecciones_Poblacionales-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The territories of modern-day Ecuador were once home to a variety of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">Amerindian</a> groups that were gradually incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a> during the 15th century. The territory was <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">colonized by Spain</a> during the 16th century, achieving independence in 1820 as part of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a>, from which it emerged as its own sovereign state in 1830. The legacy of both empires is reflected in Ecuador's ethnically diverse population, with most of its 17.1 million people being <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizos</a>, followed by large minorities of European, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">Native American</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Afro-Ecuadorians" title="Afro-Ecuadorians">African</a> descendants. <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> is the official language and is spoken by a majority of the population, though 13 Native languages are also recognized, including <a href="/wiki/Quechuan_languages" title="Quechuan languages">Quechua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shuar_language" title="Shuar language">Shuar</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Ecuador is a middle-income <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic and a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> that is highly dependent on commodities, namely petroleum and agricultural products. It is governed as a democratic <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> republic. The country is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forum_for_the_Progress_and_Development_of_South_America" title="Forum for the Progress and Development of South America">PROSUR</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. </p>
      <p>One of 17 <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a> in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Conservation_International_Site_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conservation_International_Site-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Ecuador hosts many <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> plants and animals, such as those of the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a>. In recognition of its unique ecological heritage, the new constitution of 2008 is the first in the world to recognize legally enforceable <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_Nature" class="mw-redirect" title="Rights of Nature">Rights of Nature</a>, or ecosystem rights.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Economic_and_Policy_Research" title="Center for Economic and Policy Research">Center for Economic and Policy Research</a>, between 2006 and 2016, poverty decreased from 36.7% to 22.5% and annual per capita GDP growth was 1.5 percent (as compared to 0.6 percent over the prior two decades). At the same time, the country's Gini index of economic inequality decreased from 0.55 to 0.47.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The country's name means "<a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>" in Spanish, truncated from the Spanish official name, <i>República del Ecuador</i> (<abbr title="literally">lit.</abbr> "Republic of the Equator"), derived from the former <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_Department" title="Ecuador Department">Ecuador Department</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a> established in 1824 as a division of the former territory of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Audience_of_Quito" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Audience of Quito">Royal Audience of Quito</a>. Quito, which remained the capital of the department and republic, is located only about 40 kilometres (25&nbsp;mi), ¼ of a <a href="/wiki/Latitude#Subdivisions" title="Latitude">degree</a>, south of the equator. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ecuador" title="History of Ecuador">History of Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">Indigenous peoples in Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Inca_era">Pre-Inca era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-Inca era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg/170px-Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg/255px-Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg/340px-Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tolita_mythological_figure_in_feathered_costume_IMJ_B77.0161.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/History_of_Ecuador#La_Tolita_culture" title="History of Ecuador">Tumaco-La Tolita</a> mythological figure in feathered costume. Between 100 BC and 100 AD. Found in <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas,_Ecuador" title="Esmeraldas, Ecuador">Esmeraldas</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Various peoples had settled in the area of future Ecuador before the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Incas" class="mw-redirect" title="Incas">Incas</a>. The archeological evidence suggests that the <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleo-Indians</a>' first dispersal into the Americas occurred near the end of the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>, around 16,500–13,000 years ago. The first Indians who reached Ecuador may have journeyed by land from North and Central America or by boat down the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> coastline. Much later migrations to Ecuador may have come via the Amazon tributaries, others descended from northern <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, and others ascended from the southern part of South America through the Andes. They developed different languages while emerging as unique ethnic groups. </p>
      <p>Even though their languages were unrelated, these groups developed similar groups of cultures, each based in different environments. The people of the coast developed a fishing, hunting, and gathering culture; the people of the highland Andes developed a sedentary agricultural way of life, and the people of the Amazon basin developed a nomadic hunting-and-gathering mode of existence. </p>
      <p>Over time these groups began to interact and intermingle with each other so that groups of families in one area became one community or tribe, with a similar language and culture. Many civilizations arose in Ecuador, such as the <a href="/wiki/Valdivia_Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Valdivia Culture">Valdivia Culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machalilla_Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Machalilla Culture">Machalilla Culture</a> on the coast, the <a href="/wiki/Quitus" class="mw-redirect" title="Quitus">Quitus</a> (near present-day Quito), and the <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ari" title="Cañari">Cañari</a> (near present-day <a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">Cuenca</a>). Each civilisation developed its own distinctive architecture, pottery, and religious interests. </p>
      <p>In the highland Andes mountains, where life was more sedentary, groups of tribes cooperated and formed villages; thus the first nations based on agricultural resources and the domestication of animals formed. Eventually, through wars and marriage alliances of their <a href="/wiki/Leader" class="mw-redirect" title="Leader">leaders</a>, a group of nations formed confederations. One region consolidated under a confederation called the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Shyris&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Shyris (page does not exist)">Shyris</a>, which exercised organized trading and bartering between the different regions. Its political and military power came under the rule of the Duchicela blood-line. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inca_era">Inca era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Inca era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg/220px-Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg/330px-Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg/440px-Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1720" data-file-height="1148"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ecuador_ingapirca_inca_ruins.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ruins of <a href="/wiki/Ingapirca" title="Ingapirca">Ingapirca</a>, this site served as an outpost and provisioning of the Incan troops, but mainly it was a place of worship and veneration to the sun, the supreme Inca God, thus constituting a <a href="/wiki/Coricancha" title="Coricancha">Coricancha</a>, dedicated to the Inca ritual.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg/170px-M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg/255px-M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg/340px-M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1715" data-file-height="1745"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BAmia_de_cabe%C3%A7a_-_Povo_Jivaro_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Pre-Hispanic shrunken head of the <a href="/wiki/Shuar" title="Shuar">Shuars</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jivaroan_peoples" title="Jivaroan peoples">Jivaroan peoples</a>).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>When the <a href="/wiki/Incas" class="mw-redirect" title="Incas">Incas</a> arrived, they found that these confederations were so developed that it took the Incas two generations of rulers—<a href="/wiki/Topa_Inca_Yupanqui" title="Topa Inca Yupanqui">Topa Inca Yupanqui</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huayna_Capac" title="Huayna Capac">Huayna Capac</a>—to absorb them into the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a>. The native confederations that gave them the most problems were deported to distant areas of Peru, Bolivia, and north Argentina. Similarly, a number of loyal Inca subjects from Peru and Bolivia were brought to Ecuador to prevent rebellion. Thus, the region of highland Ecuador became part of the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a> in 1463 sharing the same language. </p>
      <p>In contrast, when the Incas made incursions into coastal Ecuador and the eastern Amazon jungles of Ecuador, they found both the environment and indigenous people more hostile. Moreover, when the Incas tried to subdue them, these indigenous people withdrew to the interior and resorted to <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla">guerrilla</a> tactics. As a result, Inca expansion into the Amazon Basin and the Pacific coast of Ecuador was hampered. The indigenous people of the Amazon jungle and coastal Ecuador remained relatively autonomous until the Spanish soldiers and missionaries arrived in force. The Amazonian people and the <a href="/wiki/Chachi_people" title="Chachi people">Cayapas</a> of Coastal Ecuador were the only groups to resist Inca and Spanish domination, maintaining their language and culture well into the 21st century. </p>
      <p>Before the arrival of the Spaniards, the Inca Empire was involved in a <a href="/wiki/Inca_Civil_War" title="Inca Civil War">civil war</a>. The untimely death of both the heir Ninan Cuchi and the Emperor Huayna Capac, from a European disease that spread into Ecuador, created a power vacuum between two factions. The northern faction headed by Atahualpa claimed that Huayna Capac gave a verbal decree before his death about how the empire should be divided. He gave the territories pertaining to present-day Ecuador and northern Peru to his favorite son Atahualpa, who was to rule from Quito; and he gave the rest to <a href="/wiki/Hu%C3%A1scar" title="Huáscar">Huáscar</a>, who was to rule from <a href="/wiki/Cuzco" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuzco">Cuzco</a>. He willed that his heart be buried in Quito, his favorite city, and the rest of his body be buried with his ancestors in Cuzco. </p>
      <p>Huáscar did not recognize his father's will, since it did not follow Inca traditions of naming an Inca through the priests. Huáscar ordered Atahualpa to attend their father's burial in Cuzco and pay homage to him as the new Inca ruler. Atahualpa, with a large number of his father's veteran soldiers, decided to ignore Huáscar, and a civil war ensued. A number of bloody battles took place until finally Huáscar was captured. Atahualpa marched south to Cuzco and massacred the royal family associated with his brother. </p>
      <p>In 1532, a small band of Spaniards headed by Francisco Pizarro landed in Tumbez and marched over the Andes Mountains until they reached Cajamarca, where the new Inca Atahualpa was to hold an interview with them. Valverde, the priest, tried to convince Atahualpa that he should join the Catholic Church and declare himself a vassal of Spain. This infuriated Atahualpa so much that he threw the Bible to the ground. At this point the enraged Spaniards, with orders from Valverde, attacked and massacred unarmed escorts of the Inca and captured Atahualpa. <a href="/wiki/Pizarro" class="mw-redirect" title="Pizarro">Pizarro</a> promised to release Atahualpa if he made good his promise of filling a room full of gold. But, after a mock trial, the Spaniards executed Atahualpa by strangulation. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_colonization">Spanish colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spanish colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_principal_de_Quito,_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_(Museo_de_la_Moneda,_Bogot%C3%A1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Plaza_principal_de_Quito%2C_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_%28Museo_de_la_Moneda%2C_Bogot%C3%A1%29.jpg/220px-Plaza_principal_de_Quito%2C_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_%28Museo_de_la_Moneda%2C_Bogot%C3%A1%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Plaza_principal_de_Quito%2C_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_%28Museo_de_la_Moneda%2C_Bogot%C3%A1%29.jpg/330px-Plaza_principal_de_Quito%2C_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_%28Museo_de_la_Moneda%2C_Bogot%C3%A1%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Plaza_principal_de_Quito%2C_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_%28Museo_de_la_Moneda%2C_Bogot%C3%A1%29.jpg/440px-Plaza_principal_de_Quito%2C_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_%28Museo_de_la_Moneda%2C_Bogot%C3%A1%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="926" data-file-height="686"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_principal_de_Quito,_an%C3%B3nimo_-_siglo_XVIII_(Museo_de_la_Moneda,_Bogot%C3%A1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Major square of Quito. Painting of 18th century. <a href="/wiki/Quito_School" title="Quito School">Quito Painting Colonial School</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>New infectious diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, endemic to the Europeans, caused high fatalities among the Amerindian population during the first decades of Spanish rule, as they had no <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">immunity</a>. At the same time, the natives were forced into the <i><a href="/wiki/Encomienda" title="Encomienda">encomienda</a></i> labor system for the Spanish. In 1563, <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> became the seat of a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Audience_of_Quito" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Audience of Quito">real audiencia</a> (administrative district) of Spain and part of the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Viceroyalty of Peru</a> and later the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/1797_Riobamba_earthquake" title="1797 Riobamba earthquake">1797 Riobamba earthquake</a>, which caused up to 40,000 casualties, was studied by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a>, when he visited the area in 1801–1802.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After nearly 300 years of Spanish rule, Quito was still a small city numbering 10,000 inhabitants. On August 10, 1809, the city's <i><a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">criollos</a></i> called for independence from Spain (first among the peoples of Latin America). They were led by Juan Pío Montúfar, Quiroga, Salinas, and Bishop Cuero y Caicedo. Quito's nickname, "<i><a href="/wiki/Luz_de_Am%C3%A9rica" class="mw-redirect" title="Luz de América">Luz de América</a></i>" ("Light of America"), is based on its leading role in trying to secure an independent, local government. Although the new government lasted no more than two months, it had important repercussions and was an inspiration for the independence movement of the rest of Spanish America. August 10 is now celebrated as Independence Day, a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Ecuador" title="Public holidays in Ecuador">national holiday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_War_of_Independence" title="Ecuadorian War of Independence">Ecuadorian War of Independence</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG/170px-Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG/255px-Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG/340px-Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="614"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jose_Antonio_de_Sucre.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Venezuelan independence leader <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">Antonio José de Sucre</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg/170px-Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg/255px-Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg/340px-Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="543"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Entrevista_de_Guayaquil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The "<a href="/wiki/Guayaquil_Conference" title="Guayaquil Conference">Guayaquil Conference</a>" was the meeting between the two main Hispanic South American independence leaders. In it the form of government of the nascent countries was discussed, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn" title="José de San Martín">San Martín</a> opted for a unified South America in the form of a monarchy, while <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Bolívar</a> opted for the same but into a republic. 1843 painting.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On October 9, 1820, the Department of <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a> became the first territory in Ecuador to gain its independence from Spain, and it spawned most of the Ecuadorian coastal provinces, establishing itself as an independent state. Its inhabitants celebrated what is now Ecuador's official Independence Day on May 24, 1822. The rest of Ecuador gained its independence after <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">Antonio José de Sucre</a> defeated the Spanish Royalist forces at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pichincha" title="Battle of Pichincha">Battle of Pichincha</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>. Following the battle, Ecuador joined <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Gran_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Gran Colombia">Republic of Gran Colombia</a>, also including modern-day <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>. In 1830, Ecuador separated from Gran Colombia and became an independent republic. Two years later, it annexed the <a href="/wiki/Galapagos_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Galapagos Islands">Galapagos Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 19th century was marked by instability for Ecuador with a rapid succession of rulers. The first president of Ecuador was the Venezuelan-born <a href="/wiki/Juan_Jos%C3%A9_Flores" title="Juan José Flores">Juan José Flores</a>, who was ultimately deposed, followed by several authoritarian leaders, such as <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Rocafuerte" title="Vicente Rocafuerte">Vicente Rocafuerte</a>; <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Olmedo" title="José Joaquín de Olmedo">José Joaquín de Olmedo</a>; <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Urbina" class="mw-redirect" title="José María Urbina">José María Urbina</a>; <a href="/wiki/Diego_Noboa" title="Diego Noboa">Diego Noboa</a>; <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Jos%C3%A9_de_Arteta" title="Pedro José de Arteta">Pedro José de Arteta</a>; <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Asc%C3%A1subi" title="Manuel de Ascásubi">Manuel de Ascásubi</a>; and Flores's own son, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Flores_Jij%C3%B3n" title="Antonio Flores Jijón">Antonio Flores Jijón</a>, among others. The conservative <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_Moreno" title="Gabriel García Moreno">Gabriel García Moreno</a> unified the country in the 1860s with the support of the Roman Catholic Church. In the late 19th century, world demand for <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> tied the economy to commodity exports and led to migrations from the highlands to the agricultural frontier on the coast. </p>
      <p>Ecuador <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolition of slavery timeline">abolished</a> <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Latin_America" title="Slavery in Latin America">slavery</a> and freed its <a href="/wiki/Afro-Ecuadorian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Ecuadorian">black slaves</a> in 1851.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberal_Revolution">Liberal Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Liberal Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg/220px-Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg/330px-Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg/440px-Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg 2x" data-file-width="506" data-file-height="380"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Center_of_Quito_-_World_Heritage_Site_by_UNESCO_-_Photo_437.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Antique <a href="/wiki/Dugout_(boat)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dugout (boat)">dug out canoes</a> in the courtyard of the Old Military Hospital in the <a href="/wiki/Historic_Center_of_Quito" class="mw-redirect" title="Historic Center of Quito">Historic Center of Quito</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Revolution_of_1895" title="Liberal Revolution of 1895">Liberal Revolution of 1895</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Liberal Revolution of 1895 under <a href="/wiki/Eloy_Alfaro" title="Eloy Alfaro">Eloy Alfaro</a> reduced the power of the clergy and the conservative land owners. This liberal wing retained power until the military "Julian Revolution" of 1925. The 1930s and 1940s were marked by instability and emergence of populist politicians, such as five-time President <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Velasco_Ibarra" title="José María Velasco Ibarra">José María Velasco Ibarra</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_claimed_territories_since_1830">Loss of claimed territories since 1830</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Loss of claimed territories since 1830">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Ecuadorian%E2%80%93Peruvian_territorial_dispute" title="History of the Ecuadorian–Peruvian territorial dispute">History of the Ecuadorian–Peruvian territorial dispute</a>
      </div>
