       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador has a total area of 283,561&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (109,484&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), including the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a>. Of this, 276,841&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (106,889&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) is land and 6,720&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (2,595&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) water.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Ecuador is bigger than Uruguay, Suriname, Guyana and French Guiana in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>. </p>
      <p>Ecuador lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_north" title="2nd parallel north">2°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_south" title="5th parallel south">5°S</a>, bounded on the west by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, and has 2,337&nbsp;km (1,452&nbsp;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Coastline" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastline">coastline</a>. It has 2,010&nbsp;km (1,250&nbsp;mi) of land boundaries, with <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> in the north (with a 590&nbsp;km (367&nbsp;mi) border) and Peru in the east and south (with a 1,420&nbsp;km (882&nbsp;mi) border). It is the westernmost country that lies on the equator.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country has four main geographic regions: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>La Costa</b>, or "the coast": The coastal region consists of the provinces to the west of the Andean range&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_Province" title="Esmeraldas Province">Esmeraldas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayas_Province" title="Guayas Province">Guayas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_R%C3%ADos_Province" title="Los Ríos Province">Los Ríos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manab%C3%AD_Province" title="Manabí Province">Manabí</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Oro_Province" title="El Oro Province">El Oro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Province" title="Santa Elena Province">Santa Elena</a>. It is the country's most fertile and productive land, and is the seat of the large <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> exportation plantations of the companies <a href="/wiki/Dole_Food_Company" title="Dole Food Company">Dole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chiquita" class="mw-redirect" title="Chiquita">Chiquita</a>. This region is also where most of Ecuador's <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> crop is grown. The truly coastal provinces have active fisheries. The largest coastal city is <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>.</li> 
       <li><b>La Sierra</b>, or "the highlands": The sierra consists of the Andean and Interandean highland provinces&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Azuay_Province" title="Azuay Province">Azuay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ar_Province" title="Cañar Province">Cañar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carchi_Province" title="Carchi Province">Carchi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo_Province" title="Chimborazo Province">Chimborazo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imbabura_Province" title="Imbabura Province">Imbabura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loja_Province" title="Loja Province">Loja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province" title="Pichincha Province">Pichincha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tungurahua_Province" title="Tungurahua Province">Tungurahua</a>. This land contains most of Ecuador's volcanoes and all of its snow-capped peaks. Agriculture is focused on the traditional crops of <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quinoa" title="Quinoa">quinua</a> and the population is predominantly Amerindian <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Kichua</a>. The largest Sierran city is <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>.</li> 
       <li><b>La Amazonía</b>, also known as <i>El Oriente</i>, or "the east": The oriente consists of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon jungle</a> provinces&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Morona_Santiago_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Morona Santiago Province">Morona Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napo_Province" title="Napo Province">Napo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orellana_Province" title="Orellana Province">Orellana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pastaza_Province" title="Pastaza Province">Pastaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sucumb%C3%ADos_Province" title="Sucumbíos Province">Sucumbíos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zamora-Chinchipe_Province" title="Zamora-Chinchipe Province">Zamora-Chinchipe</a>. This region is primarily made up of the huge Amazon national parks and Amerindian untouchable zones, which are vast stretches of land set aside for the Amazon Amerindian tribes to continue living traditionally. It is also the area with the largest reserves of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> in Ecuador, and parts of the upper Amazon here have been extensively exploited by petroleum companies. The population is primarily mixed Amerindian <a href="/wiki/Shuar" title="Shuar">Shuar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huaorani" class="mw-redirect" title="Huaorani">Huaorani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Kichua</a>, although there are numerous tribes in the deep jungle which are little-contacted. The largest city in the Oriente is probably <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Loja" title="Nueva Loja">Lago Agrio</a> in Sucumbíos, although <a href="/wiki/Macas_(city)" title="Macas (city)">Macas</a> in Morona Santiago runs a close second.</li> 
       <li><b>La Región Insular</b> is the region comprising the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a>, some 1,000 kilometres (620&nbsp;mi) west of the mainland in the Pacific Ocean.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Ecuador's capital is Quito, which is in the province of <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_Province,_Ecuador" class="mw-redirect" title="Pichincha Province, Ecuador">Pichincha</a> in the Sierra region. Its largest city is Guayaquil, in the <a href="/wiki/Guayas_Province" title="Guayas Province">Guayas Province</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">Cotopaxi</a>, just south of Quito, is one of the world's highest active volcanoes. The top of <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo_(volcano)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chimborazo (volcano)">Mount Chimborazo</a> (6,268 m, or 20,560&nbsp;ft, above sea level), Ecuador's tallest mountain, is the most distant point from the center of the Earth on the Earth's surface because of the <a href="/wiki/Ellipsoid" title="Ellipsoid">ellipsoid</a> shape of the planet.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Ecuador" title="Climate of Ecuador">Climate of Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="103" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1816" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_ECU_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ecuador map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There is great variety in the climate, largely determined by altitude. It is mild year-round in the mountain valleys, with a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> in coastal areas and <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> in lowlands. The Pacific coastal area has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> with a severe rainy season. The climate in the Andean highlands is <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperateness">temperate</a> and relatively dry, and the Amazon basin on the eastern side of the mountains shares the climate of other rainforest zones. </p>
      <p>Because of its location at the equator, Ecuador experiences little variation in daylight hours during the course of a year. Both sunrise and sunset occur each day at the two six o'clock hours.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">Hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rivers_of_Ecuador" class="mw-redirect" title="Rivers of Ecuador">Rivers of Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG/170px-Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG/255px-Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG/340px-Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG 2x" data-file-width="486" data-file-height="648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Canyoning_en_Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa" title="Baños de Agua Santa">Baños de Agua Santa</a> is an important tourist site
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Andes is the <i>watershed divisor</i> between the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Basin">Amazon</a> watershed, which runs to the east, and the Pacific, including the north–south rivers Mataje, Santiago, <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas_River" title="Esmeraldas River">Esmeraldas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chone_River" title="Chone River">Chone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayas_River" title="Guayas River">Guayas</a>, Jubones, and Puyango-Tumbes. </p>
      <p>Almost all of the rivers in Ecuador form in the Sierra region and flow east toward the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a> or west toward the Pacific Ocean. The rivers rise from snowmelt at the edges of the snowcapped peaks or from the abundant precipitation that falls at higher elevations. In the Sierra region, the streams and rivers are narrow and flow rapidly over precipitous slopes. Rivers may slow and widen as they cross the hoyas yet become rapid again as they flow from the heights of the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> to the lower elevations of the other regions. The highland rivers broaden as they enter the more level areas of the Costa and the Oriente. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg/220px-Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg/330px-Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg/440px-Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Driving_the_beach_salinas_ecuador.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A beach of <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Ecuador" title="Salinas, Ecuador">Salinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Province" title="Santa Elena Province">Santa Elena Province</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the Costa, the external coast has mostly intermittent rivers that are fed by constant rains from December through May and become empty riverbeds during the dry season. The few exceptions are the longer, perennial rivers that flow throughout the external coast from the internal coast and La Sierra on their way to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. The internal coast, by contrast, is crossed by perennial rivers that may flood during the rainy season, sometimes forming swamps. </p>
      <p>Major rivers in the Oriente include the <a href="/wiki/Pastaza_River" title="Pastaza River">Pastaza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napo_River" title="Napo River">Napo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Putumayo_River" title="Putumayo River">Putumayo</a>. The Pastaza is formed by the confluence of the Chambo and the Patate rivers, both of which rise in the Sierra. The Pastaza includes the Agoyan waterfall, which at sixty-one meters (200 feet) is the highest waterfall in Ecuador. The Napo rises near Mount Cotopaxi and is the major river used for transport in the eastern lowlands. The Napo ranges in width from 500 to 1,800&nbsp;m (1,640 to 5,906&nbsp;ft). In its upper reaches, the Napo flows rapidly until the confluence with one of its major tributaries, the Coca River, where it slows and levels off. The Putumayo forms part of the border with Colombia. All of these rivers flow into the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a>. The Galápagos Islands have no significant rivers. Several of the larger islands, however, have freshwater springs, although they are surrounded by the Pacific Ocean. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg/200px-Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg/300px-Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg/400px-Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2851" data-file-height="2142"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oso_andino_Porcon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ecuador is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a> in the world, it also has the most biodiversity per square kilometer of any nation, and is one of the highest <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemism</a> worldwide. In the image the <a href="/wiki/Spectacled_bear" title="Spectacled bear">Spectacled bear</a> of the Andes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador is one of seventeen <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a> in the world according to Conservation International,<sup id="cite_ref-Conservation_International_Site_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conservation_International_Site-19">[19]</a></sup> and it has the most biodiversity per square kilometer of any nation.<sup id="cite_ref-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ecuador has 1,600 bird species (15% of the world's known bird species) in the continental area and 38 more <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> in the Galápagos. In addition to more than 16,000 species of plants, the country has 106 endemic reptiles, 138 endemic amphibians, and 6,000 species of butterfly. The Galápagos Islands are well known as a region of distinct fauna, as the famous place of birth to Darwin's <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_Evolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Theory of Evolution">Theory of Evolution</a>, and as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage Site.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest,_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest%2C_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg/220px-Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest%2C_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest%2C_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg/330px-Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest%2C_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest%2C_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg/440px-Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest%2C_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1936"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ecuadorian_Amazon_rain_forest,_looking_toward_the_Andes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a> in Ecuador
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador has the first constitution to recognize the <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_Nature" class="mw-redirect" title="Rights of Nature">rights of nature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The protection of the nation's biodiversity is an explicit national priority as stated in the National Plan of "Buen Vivir", or good living, Objective 4, "Guarantee the rights of nature", Policy 1: "Sustainably conserve and manage the natural heritage, including its land and marine biodiversity, which is considered a strategic sector".<sup id="cite_ref-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of the writing of the plan in 2008, 19% of Ecuador's land area was in a protected area; however, the plan also states that 32% of the land must be protected in order to truly preserve the nation's biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Plan_Nacional_del_Buen_Vivir-64">[64]</a></sup> Current <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_Ecuador" title="List of national parks in Ecuador">protected areas</a> include 11 national parks, 10 wildlife refuges, 9 ecological reserves, and other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> A program begun in 2008, Sociobosque, is preserving another 2.3% of total land area (6,295&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>, or 629,500 ha) by paying private landowners or community landowners (such as Amerindian tribes) incentives to maintain their land as native ecosystems such as native forests or grasslands. Eligibility and subsidy rates for this program are determined based on the poverty in the region, the number of hectares that will be protected, and the type of ecosystem of the land to be protected, among other factors.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Ecuador had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.66/10, ranking it 35th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-70">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite being on the UNESCO list, the Galápagos are endangered by a range of negative environmental effects, threatening the existence of this exotic <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Petroecuador" title="Petroecuador">oil exploitation of the Amazon rainforest</a> has led to the release of billions of gallons of untreated wastes, gas, and crude oil into the environment,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> contaminating ecosystems and causing detrimental health effects to Amerindian peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> One of the best known examples is the <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Texaco-Chevron</a> case.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> This American <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_in_the_United_States" title="Petroleum in the United States">oil company</a> operated in the Ecuadorian Amazon region between 1964 and 1992. During this period, Texaco drilled 339 wells in 15 petroleum fields and abandoned 627 toxic wastewater pits, as well as other elements of the oil infrastructure. It is now known that these highly polluting and now obsolete technologies were used as a way to reduce expenses.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Ecuador" title="Economy of Ecuador">Economy of Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/220px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/330px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png/440px-Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png 2x" data-file-width="932" data-file-height="954"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Products_exported_by_Ecuador.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tree map of products exported by Ecuador in the HS4 product classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador has a <a href="/wiki/Developing_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing economy">developing economy</a> that is highly dependent on commodities, namely petroleum and agricultural products. The country is classified as an upper-middle-income country. Ecuador's economy is the eighth largest in Latin America and experienced an average growth of 4.6% between 2000 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2019)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> From 2007 to 2012, Ecuador's GDP grew at an annual average of 4.3 percent, above the average for Latin America and the Caribbean, which was 3.5%, according to the United Nations' Economic Commission for Latin American and the Caribbean (ECLAC).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Ecuador was able to maintain relatively superior growth during the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">crisis</a>. In January 2009, the Central Bank of Ecuador (BCE) put the 2010 growth forecast at 6.88%.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In 2011, its GDP grew at 8% and ranked 3rd highest in Latin America, behind Argentina (2nd) and Panama (1st).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Between 1999 and 2007, GDP doubled, reaching $65,490 million according to BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The inflation rate until January 2008, was about 1.14%, the highest in the past year, according to the government.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The monthly unemployment rate remained at about 6 and 8 percent from December 2007 until September 2008; however, it went up to about 9 percent in October and dropped again in November 2008 to 8 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Unemployment mean annual rate for 2009 in Ecuador was 8.5% because the global economic crisis continued to affect the Latin American economies. From this point, unemployment rates started a downward trend: 7.6% in 2010, 6.0% in 2011, and 4.8% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The extreme poverty rate has declined significantly between 1999 and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In 2001, it was estimated at 40% of the population, while by 2011 the figure dropped to 17.4% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-87">[87]</a></sup> This is explained to an extent by emigration and the economic stability achieved after adopting the U.S. dollar as official means of transaction (before 2000, the Ecuadorian <i><a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_sucre" title="Ecuadorian sucre">sucre</a></i> was prone to rampant inflation). However, starting in 2008, with the bad economic performance of the nations where most Ecuadorian emigrants work, the reduction of poverty has been realized through social spending, mainly in education and health.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Obverse_of_the_series_2009_$100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg/250px-Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg/375px-Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg/500px-Obverse_of_the_series_2009_%24100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="505"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Obverse_of_the_series_2009_$100_Federal_Reserve_Note.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> is the common currency circulation in Ecuador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oil accounts for 40% of exports and contributes to maintaining a positive trade balance.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Since the late 1960s, the exploitation of oil increased production, and proven reserves are estimated at 6.51 billion barrels as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The overall trade balance for August 2012 was a surplus of almost $390 million for the first six months of 2012, a huge figure compared with that of 2007, which reached only $5.7 million; the surplus had risen by about $425 million compared to 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-87">[87]</a></sup> The oil trade balance positive had revenues of $3.295 million in 2008, while non-oil was negative, amounting to $2.842 million. The trade balance with the United States, Chile, the European Union, Bolivia, Peru, Brazil, and Mexico is positive. The trade balance with Argentina, Colombia, and Asia is negative.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the agricultural sector, Ecuador is a major exporter of bananas (first place worldwide in production and export), flowers, and the seventh largest producer of cocoa.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Ecuador also produces coffee, rice, potatoes, cassava (manioc, tapioca), plantains and sugarcane; cattle, sheep, pigs, beef, pork and dairy products; fish, and shrimp; and balsa wood.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The country's vast resources include large amounts of timber across the country, like eucalyptus and mangroves.<sup id="cite_ref-Resources_Maps_World_Banks_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resources_Maps_World_Banks-94">[94]</a></sup> Pines and cedars are planted in the region of La Sierra and walnuts, rosemary, and balsa wood in the Guayas River Basin.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The industry is concentrated mainly in Guayaquil, the largest industrial center, and in Quito, where in recent years the industry has grown considerably. This city is also the largest business center of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Industrial production is directed primarily to the domestic market.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Despite this, there is limited export of products produced or processed industrially.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These include canned foods, liquor, jewelry, furniture, and more.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A minor industrial activity is also concentrated in Cuenca.<sup id="cite_ref-Industrias_en_Cuenca_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Industrias_en_Cuenca-97">[97]</a></sup> Incomes from tourism has been increasing during the last few years because of the Government showing the variety of climates and the biodiversity of Ecuador. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Wtcgye.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/180px-Wtcgye.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/270px-Wtcgye.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Wtcgye.jpg/360px-Wtcgye.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2892" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Wtcgye.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>World Trade Center headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador has negotiated bilateral treaties with other countries, besides belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Community_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Andean Community of Nations">Andean Community of Nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and an associate member of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> It also serves on the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">Inter-American Development Bank</a> (IDB), <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), <a href="/wiki/Corporaci%C3%B3n_Andina_de_Fomento" class="mw-redirect" title="Corporación Andina de Fomento">Corporación Andina de Fomento</a> (CAF) and other multilateral agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In April 2007, Ecuador paid off its debt to the IMF, thus ending an era of interventionism of the Agency in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The public finance of Ecuador consists of the Central Bank of Ecuador (BCE), the National Development Bank (BNF), the State Bank. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Ecuador" title="Tourism in Ecuador">Tourism in Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Roof_deck_(Palacio_de_Pizarro),_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_(Quito),_pic.aa4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg/220px-Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg/330px-Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg/440px-Roof_deck_%28Palacio_de_Pizarro%29%2C_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_%28Quito%29%2C_pic.aa4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roof_deck_(Palacio_de_Pizarro),_Plaza_de_la_Independencia_(Quito),_pic.aa4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The historic center of <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> has one of the largest and best-preserved historic centers in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The city also houses a large number of museums.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MISAHUALLI_(19783859780).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/MISAHUALLI_%2819783859780%29.jpg/220px-MISAHUALLI_%2819783859780%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/MISAHUALLI_%2819783859780%29.jpg/330px-MISAHUALLI_%2819783859780%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/MISAHUALLI_%2819783859780%29.jpg/440px-MISAHUALLI_%2819783859780%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MISAHUALLI_(19783859780).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Animals in <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Misahuall%C3%AD" class="extiw" title="es:Puerto Misahuallí">Misahualli</a>, Ecuadorian Amazon
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Ministry of Information and Tourism was created on August 10, 1992, at the beginning of the government of <a href="/wiki/Sixto_Dur%C3%A1n_Ball%C3%A9n" title="Sixto Durán Ballén">Sixto Durán Ballén</a>, who viewed tourism as a fundamental activity for the economic and social development of the peoples. Faced with the growth of the tourism sector, in June 1994, the decision was taken to separate tourism from information, so that it is exclusively dedicated to promoting and strengthening this activity. </p>
      <p>Ecuador is a country with vast natural wealth. The diversity of its four regions has given rise to thousands of species of flora and fauna. It has approximately 1640 kinds of birds. The species of butterflies border 4,500, the reptiles 345, the amphibians 358, and the mammals 258, among others. Not in vain, Ecuador is considered one of the 17 countries where the planet's highest biodiversity is concentrated, being also the largest country with diversity per km2 in the world. Most of its fauna and flora lives in 26 protected areas by the state. </p>
      <p>Also, it has a huge culture spectrum. Since 2007, with the government of Rafael Correa, the tourism brand "Ecuador Ama la Vida" has been transformed, with which the nation's tourism promotion would be sold. Focused on considering it as a country friendly and respectful of nature, natural biodiversity, and cultural diversity of the peoples. And for this, means of exploiting them are developed along with the private economy. </p>
      <p>The country has two cities with UNESCO World Heritage Sites: Quito and Cuenca, as well as two natural UNESCO World Heritage Sites: the Galapagos Islands and Sangay National Park in addition to one <a href="/wiki/World_Network_of_Biosphere_Reserves" title="World Network of Biosphere Reserves">World Biosphere Reserve</a>, such as the Cajas Massif. Culturally, the Toquilla straw hat and the culture of the Zapara indigenous people are recognized. The most popular sites for national and foreign tourists have different nuances due to the various tourist activities offered by the country. </p>
      <p>Among the main tourist destinations are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Nature attractions: <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yasuni_National_Park" title="Yasuni National Park">Yasuni National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Cajas_National_Park" title="El Cajas National Park">El Cajas National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sangay_National_Park" title="Sangay National Park">Sangay National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Podocarpus_National_Park" title="Podocarpus National Park">Podocarpus National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vilcabamba,_Ecuador" title="Vilcabamba, Ecuador">Vilcabamba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ba%C3%B1os_de_Agua_Santa" title="Baños de Agua Santa">Baños de Agua Santa</a>.</li> 
       <li>Cultural attractions: <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Historic center of Quito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Mitad_del_Mundo" title="Ciudad Mitad del Mundo">Ciudad Mitad del Mundo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ingapirca" title="Ingapirca">Ingapirca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">Historic center of Cuenca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latacunga" title="Latacunga">Latacunga</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Mama_Negra" title="Mama Negra">Mama Negra</a> festival.</li> 
       <li>Snowy mountains: <a href="/wiki/Antisana" title="Antisana">Antisana</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Cayambe_(volcano)" title="Cayambe (volcano)">Cayambe</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo" title="Chimborazo">Chimborazo</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Cotopaxi" title="Cotopaxi">Cotopaxi</a> volcano, <a href="/wiki/Illiniza" title="Illiniza">Illinizas</a> volcanoes.</li> 
       <li>Beaches: <a href="/wiki/Atacames" title="Atacames">Atacames</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_de_Car%C3%A1quez" title="Bahía de Caráquez">Bahía de Caráquez</a>, Crucita, <a href="/wiki/Esmeraldas,_Ecuador" title="Esmeraldas, Ecuador">Esmeraldas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manta,_Ecuador" title="Manta, Ecuador">Manta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1ita" title="Montañita">Montañita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Playas,_Ecuador" title="Playas, Ecuador">Playas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Ecuador" title="Salinas, Ecuador">Salinas</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/220px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/330px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg/440px-Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1738" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Quito_Trole_06_2011_1933.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Quito" title="Trolleybuses in Quito">Trolebús</a> bus rapid transit system that runs through <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>. It is the principal BRT in Ecuador.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Ecuador.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/220px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/330px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Railways_in_Ecuador.svg/440px-Railways_in_Ecuador.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="588" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Ecuador.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Railways in Ecuador <span class="nowrap">(<a href="//sharemap.org/public/Railways_in_Ecuador" class="extiw" title="sharemap:public/Railways in Ecuador">interactive map</a>)</span>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Ecuador" title="Transport in Ecuador">Transport in Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The rehabilitation and reopening of the Ecuadorian railroad and use of it as a tourist attraction is one of the recent developments in transportation matters.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The roads of Ecuador in recent years have undergone important improvement. The major routes are Pan American (under enhancement from four to six lanes from Rumichaca to Ambato, the conclusion of 4 lanes on the entire stretch of Ambato and Riobamba and running via Riobamba to Loja). In the absence of the section between Loja and the border with Peru, there are the Route Espondilus and/or Ruta del Sol (oriented to travel along the Ecuadorian coastline) and the Amazon backbone (which crosses from north to south along the Ecuadorian Amazon, linking most and more major cities of it). </p>
      <p>Another major project is developing the road Manta – Tena, the highway Guayaquil – Salinas Highway Aloag Santo Domingo, Riobamba – Macas (which crosses Sangay National Park). Other new developments include the National Unity bridge complex in Guayaquil, the bridge over the Napo river in Francisco de Orellana, the Esmeraldas River Bridge in the city of the same name, and, perhaps the most remarkable of all, the Bahia – San Vincente Bridge, being the largest on the Latin American Pacific coast. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">Cuenca</a>'s tramway is the largest public transport system in the city and the first modern tramway in Ecuador. It was inaugurated on March 8, 2019. It has 20.4 kilometres (12.7&nbsp;mi) and 27 stations. It will transport 120,000 passagers daily. Its route starts in the south of Cuenca and ends in the north at the Parque Industrial neighbourhood. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mariscal_Sucre_International_Airport" title="Mariscal Sucre International Airport">Mariscal Sucre International Airport</a> in Quito and the <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Joaqu%C3%ADn_de_Olmedo_International_Airport" title="José Joaquín de Olmedo International Airport">José Joaquín de Olmedo International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a> have experienced a high increase in demand and have required modernization. In the case of Guayaquil it involved a new air terminal, once considered the best in South America and the best in Latin America<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and in Quito where an entire new airport has been built in Tababela and was inaugurated in February 2013, with Canadian assistance. However, the main road leading from Quito city centre to the new airport will only be finished in late 2014, making current travelling from the airport to downtown Quito as long as two hours during rush hour.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Quito's old city-centre airport is being turned into parkland, with some light industrial use. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecuadorian people">Ecuadorian people</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador's population is ethnically diverse and the 2018 estimates put Ecuador's population at 17,084,358.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-110">[110]</a></sup> The largest ethnic group (as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) is the <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizos</a></i>, who are Amerindians with mixture or cultural influence from Spanish colonists, and constitute about 71% of the population (although including the <a href="/wiki/Montubio" title="Montubio">Montubio</a>, a term used for coastal Mestizo population, brings this up to about 79%). The White Ecuadorians (<a href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White Latin American">White Latin American</a>) are a minority accounting for 6.1% of the population of Ecuador and can be found throughout all of Ecuador, primarily around the urban areas. Even though Ecuador's white population during its colonial era were mainly descendants from Spain, today Ecuador's white population is a result of a mixture of European immigrants, predominantly from Spain with people from Italy, Germany, France, and Switzerland who have settled in the early 20th century. In addition, there is a small European Jewish (<a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecuadorian Jews">Ecuadorian Jews</a>) population, which is based mainly in Quito and to a lesser extent in Guayaquil.<sup id="cite_ref-ethn_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethn-3">[3]</a></sup> Ecuador also has a small population of Asian origins, mainly those from West Asia, like the economically well off descendants of Lebanese and Palestinian immigrants, who are either Christian or Muslim (see <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Ecuador" title="Islam in Ecuador">Islam in Ecuador</a>), and an East Asian community mainly consisting of those of Japanese and Chinese descent, whose ancestors arrived as miners, farmhands and fishermen in the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Amerindians</a> account for 7% of the current population. The mostly rural Montubio population of the coastal provinces of Ecuador, who might be classified as <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">Pardo</a> account for 7.4% of the population. The <a href="/wiki/Afro-Ecuadorian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Ecuadorian people">Afro-Ecuadorians</a> are a minority population (7%) in Ecuador, that includes the <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Mulattos</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">zambos</a></i>, and are largely based in the Esmeraldas province and to a lesser degree in the predominantly Mestizo provinces of Coastal Ecuador - Guayas and Manabi. In the Highland Andes where a predominantly Mestizo, white and Amerindian population exist, the African presence is almost non-existent except for a small community in the province of Imbabura called Chota Valley. 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a> live in Ecuador.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Ecuador" title="Religion in Ecuador">Religion in Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Ecuador (2014)<sup id="cite_ref-PewResearch_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PewResearch-112">[112]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">

          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a></td>

            <div style="background:Blue; width:79%; overflow: hidden;">

          </tr>

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>According to the Ecuadorian National Institute of Statistics and Census, 91.95% of the country's population have a religion, 7.94% are <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> and 0.11% are <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostics</a>. Among the people who have a religion, 80.44% are Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Latin_Rite" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin Rite">Latin Rite</a> (see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Roman_Catholic_dioceses_in_Ecuador" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Roman Catholic dioceses in Ecuador">List of Roman Catholic dioceses in Ecuador</a>), 11.30% are <a href="/wiki/Evangelical" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical">Evangelical</a> <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>, 1.29% are <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> and 6.97% other (mainly Jewish, Buddhists and Latter-day Saints).<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the rural parts of Ecuador, Amerindian beliefs and Catholicism are sometimes <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretized</a>. Most festivals and annual parades are based on religious celebrations, many incorporating a mixture of rites and icons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There is a small number of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christians</a>, Amerindian religions, Muslims (see <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Ecuador" title="Islam in Ecuador">Islam in Ecuador</a>), <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí</a>. According to their own estimates, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> accounts for about 1.4% of the population, or 211,165 members at the end of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> According to their own sources, in 2017 there were 92,752 <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first Jews arrived in Ecuador in the 16th and 17th centuries. Most of them are <a href="/wiki/Sephardic" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic">Sephardic</a> <a href="/wiki/Anusim" title="Anusim">Anusim</a> (<a href="/wiki/Crypto-Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Crypto-Jews">Crypto-Jews</a>) and many still speak <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">Judaeo-Spanish</a> (Ladino) language.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Today the Jewish Community of Ecuador (Comunidad Judía del Ecuador) has its seat in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> and has approximately 200 members. Nevertheless, this number is declining because young people leave the country for the United States or <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. The Community has a Jewish Center with a <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a>, a country club, and a cemetery. It supports the "Albert Einstein School", where Jewish history, religion, and <a href="/wiki/Hebrew" class="mw-redirect" title="Hebrew">Hebrew</a> classes are offered. There are very small communities in <a href="/wiki/Cuenca_(Ecuador)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuenca (Ecuador)">Cuenca</a>. The "Comunidad de Culto Israelita" reunites the Jews of <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>. This community works independently from the "Jewish Community of Ecuador" and is composed of only 30 people.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> </p>

           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:pink; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other </td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:gold; width:0.4%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.4%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The Ecuadorian constitution recognizes the "pluri-nationality" of those who want to exercise their affiliation with their native ethnic groups. Thus, in addition to <i>criollos</i>, <i>mestizos</i>, and Afro-Ecuadorians, some people belong to the Amerindian nations scattered in a few places in the coast, Quechua Andean villages, and the Amazonian jungle. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_genetics">Population genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Population genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Genealogical_DNA_test" title="Genealogical DNA test">genealogical DNA testing</a> done in 2015, the average Ecuadorian is estimated to be 52.96% <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Ecuador" title="Indigenous peoples in Ecuador">Amerindian</a>, 41.77% <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a>, and 5.26% <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_African" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan African">Sub-Saharan African</a> overall.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Prior to this, a genetic study done in 2008 by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Brasilia" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Brasilia">University of Brasilia</a>, estimated that Ecuadorian genetic admixture was 64.6% Amerindian, 31.0% European, and 4.4% African.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_density">Population density</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Population density">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The majority of Ecuadorians live in the central provinces, the Andes mountains, or along the Pacific coast. The tropical forest region to the east of the mountains (El Oriente) remains sparsely populated and contains only about 3% of the population. Birth rate is 2-1 for each death. Marriages are usually from 14 and above using parental consent. About 12.4% of the population is married in the ages 15–19. Divorce rates are moderate. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The five largest cities in the country are <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> (2.78 million inhabitants), <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a> (2.72 million inhabitants), <a href="/wiki/Cuenca,_Ecuador" title="Cuenca, Ecuador">Cuenca</a> (636,996 inhabitants), <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo_(Ecuador)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santo Domingo (Ecuador)">Santo Domingo</a> (458,580 inhabitants), and <a href="/wiki/Ambato,_Ecuador" title="Ambato, Ecuador">Ambato</a> (387,309 inhabitants). While the most populated metropolitan areas of the country are those of Guayaquil, Quito, Cuenca, Manabí Centro (<a href="/wiki/Portoviejo" title="Portoviejo">Portoviejo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Manta,_Ecuador" title="Manta, Ecuador">Manta</a>) and Ambato.<sup id="cite_ref-Proyecciones_Poblacionales_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proyecciones_Poblacionales-16">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="navbox">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration_and_emigration">Immigration and emigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Immigration and emigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Emigration_from_Ecuador" title="Emigration from Ecuador">Emigration from Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31"></a></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs expansion</b>. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>. <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2012</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>There's a small East Asian community mainly consisting of those of Japanese and Chinese descent, whose ancestors arrived as miners, farmhands and fishermen in the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early years of World War II, Ecuador still admitted a certain number of immigrants, and in 1939, when several South American countries refused to accept 165 Jewish refugees from Germany aboard the ship <i>Koenigstein</i>, Ecuador granted them entry permits.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early 1900s there was immigration from <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britons" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons">Britons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>. In the 1950s the Italians were the third largest national group in terms of numbers of immigrants, since Ecuador like Mexico and the Andean countries did not receive a significant total number of immigrants. It can be noted that, after World War I, people from Liguria, still constituted the majority of the flow, even though they then represented only one third of the total number of immigrants in Ecuador. This situation came from the improvement of the economic situation in Liguria. The classic paradigm of the Italian immigrant today was not that of the small trader from Liguria as it had been before; those who emigrated to Ecuador were professionals and technicians, employees and religious people from South-Central Italy. It must be remembered that many immigrants, a remarkable number of Italians among them, moved to the Ecuadorian port from Peru to escape from the Peruvian war with Chile. The Italian government came to be more interested in the emigration phenomenon in Ecuador because of the necessity of finding an outlet for the large number of immigrants who traditionally went to the United States but who could no longer enter this country because of the new measures that imposed restrictions in the 1920s. Most of these communities and their descendants are located in the <a href="/wiki/Guayas_Province" title="Guayas Province">Guayas</a> region of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years, Ecuador has grown in popularity among North American expatriates.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Another perk that draws many expats to Ecuador is its low cost of living. Since everything from gas to groceries costs far less than in North America, it is a popular choice for those who are looking to make the most of their retirement budget.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Ecuador" title="Culture of Ecuador">Culture of Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg/170px-Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg/255px-Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg/340px-Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2194" data-file-height="3072"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ca%C3%B1ari_people_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1ari" title="Cañari">Cañari</a> children with the typical Andean indigenous clothes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador's mainstream culture is defined by its Hispanic <i><a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a></i> majority, and, like their ancestry, it is traditionally of Spanish heritage, influenced in different degrees by Amerindian traditions and in some cases by African elements. The first and most substantial wave of modern immigration to Ecuador consisted of Spanish colonists, following the arrival of Europeans in 1499. A lower number of other Europeans and North Americans migrated to the country in the late 19th and early 20th centuries and, in smaller numbers, Poles, Lithuanians, English, Irish, and Croats during and after the Second World War. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Alicia_Cahuiya,_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Alicia_Cahuiya%2C_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg/170px-Alicia_Cahuiya%2C_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Alicia_Cahuiya%2C_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg/255px-Alicia_Cahuiya%2C_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Alicia_Cahuiya%2C_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg/340px-Alicia_Cahuiya%2C_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5520" data-file-height="3680"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Alicia_Cahuiya,_Caso_Tagaeri_y_Taromenani.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Huaorani_people" title="Huaorani people">Huaorani</a> man with the typical Amazonian indigenous clothes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since African slavery was not the workforce of the Spanish colonies in the Andes Mountains, given the subjugation of the Amerindian people through proselytization and <i><a href="/wiki/Encomiendas" class="mw-redirect" title="Encomiendas">encomiendas</a></i>, the minority population of African descent is mostly found in the coastal northern province of Esmeraldas. This is largely owing to the 17th-century shipwreck of a slave-trading galleon off the northern coast of Ecuador. The few African survivors swam to the shore and penetrated the then-thick jungle under the leadership of Anton, the chief of the group, where they remained as free men maintaining their original culture, not influenced by the typical elements found in other provinces of the coast or in the Andean region. A little later, freed slaves from Colombia known as <i>cimarrones</i> joined them. In the small Chota Valley of the province of Imbabura exists a small community of Africans among the province's predominantly mestizo population. These blacks are descendants of Africans, who were brought over from Colombia by Jesuits to work their colonial sugar plantations as slaves. As a general rule, small elements of zambos and mulattoes coexisted among the overwhelming mestizo population of coastal Ecuador throughout its history as gold miners in Loja, Zaruma, and Zamora and as shipbuilders and plantation workers around the city of Guayaquil. Today you can find a small community of Africans in the Catamayo valley of the predominantly mestizo population of Loja. </p>
      <p>Ecuador's Amerindian communities are integrated into the mainstream culture to varying degrees,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> but some may also practice their own native cultures, particularly the more remote Amerindian communities of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">Amazon basin</a>. Spanish is spoken as the first language by more than 90% of the population and as a first or second language by more than 98%. Part of Ecuador's population can speak <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> languages, in some cases as a second language. Two percent of the population speak only Amerindian languages. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Ecuador" title="Languages of Ecuador">Languages of Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Languages in Ecuador<sup id="cite_ref-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA-119">[119]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Language</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>

            <div style="background:Blue; width: 93%; overflow: hidden;">

           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:Orange; width:4.1%; overflow: hidden;">

          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Foreign </td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:Green; width: 2.2%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;"> 2.2%</td> 
          </tr>

           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other Indigenous </td>

            <div style="background:Red; width:0.7%; overflow: hidden;">
