          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Most Ecuadorians speak Spanish as their first language, with its ubiquity permeating and dominating most of the country, though there are many who speak an Amerindian language, such as <a href="/wiki/Kichwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Kichwa">Kichwa</a> (also spelled Quechua), which is one of the Quechuan languages and is spoken by approximately 2.5 million people in Ecuador, Bolivia, Colombia, and Peru.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Other Amerindian languages spoken in Ecuador include Awapit (spoken by the Awá), A'ingae (spoken by the Cofan), Shuar Chicham (spoken by the Shuar), Achuar-Shiwiar (spoken by the Achuar and the Shiwiar), Cha'palaachi (spoken by the Chachi), Tsa'fiki (spoken by the Tsáchila), Paicoca (spoken by the Siona and Secoya), and Wao Tededeo (spoken by the Waorani). Use of these Amerindian languages are, however, gradually diminishing due to Spanish's widespread use in education. Though most features of Ecuadorian Spanish are universal to the Spanish-speaking world, there are several idiosyncrasies. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Ecuador" title="Music of Ecuador">Music of Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg/150px-Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg/225px-Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg/300px-Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="6016"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mirella_Cesa_en_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mirella_Cesa" title="Mirella Cesa">Mirella Cesa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The music of Ecuador has a long history. <a href="/wiki/Pasillo" title="Pasillo">Pasillo</a> is a genre of indigenous Latin music. In Ecuador it is the "national genre of music". Through the years, many cultures have brought their influences together to create new types of music. There are also different kinds of traditional music like albazo, pasacalle, fox incaico, tonada, capishca, <a href="/wiki/Bomba_(Ecuador)" title="Bomba (Ecuador)">Bomba</a> (highly established in Afro-Ecuadorian societies), and so on. <a href="/wiki/Tecnocumbia" title="Tecnocumbia">Tecnocumbia</a> and Rockola are clear examples of the influence of foreign cultures. One of the most traditional forms of dancing in Ecuador is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sanjuanito&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sanjuanito (page does not exist)">Sanjuanito</a>. It is originally from northern Ecuador (<a href="/wiki/Otavalo_(city)" title="Otavalo (city)">Otavalo</a>-Imbabura). Sanjuanito is a type of dance music played during festivities by the mestizo and Amerindian communities. According to the Ecuadorian musicologist Segundo Luis Moreno, Sanjuanito was danced by Amerindian people during San Juan Bautista's birthday. This important date was established by the Spaniards on June 24, coincidentally the same date when Amerindian people celebrated their rituals of <a href="/wiki/Inti_Raymi" title="Inti Raymi">Inti Raymi</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ecuadorian_dishes_and_foods" title="List of Ecuadorian dishes and foods">List of Ecuadorian dishes and foods</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ceviche_ecuador.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ceviche_ecuador.JPG/150px-Ceviche_ecuador.JPG" decoding="async" width="150" height="113" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ceviche_ecuador.JPG/225px-Ceviche_ecuador.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Ceviche_ecuador.JPG/300px-Ceviche_ecuador.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1182" data-file-height="887"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:156px;max-width:156px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Cuy_Guinea_Pig_Dish_SG.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cuy_Guinea_Pig_Dish_SG.jpg/154px-Cuy_Guinea_Pig_Dish_SG.jpg" decoding="async" width="154" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cuy_Guinea_Pig_Dish_SG.jpg/231px-Cuy_Guinea_Pig_Dish_SG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cuy_Guinea_Pig_Dish_SG.jpg/308px-Cuy_Guinea_Pig_Dish_SG.jpg 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="455"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <i>Ceviche ecuatoriano</i> (Ecuadorian-style <a href="/wiki/Ceviche" title="Ceviche">ceviche</a>) and <i>Cuy asado</i> (grilled <a href="/wiki/Guinea_pig" title="Guinea pig">guinea pig</a>) are some of the typical dishes.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_cuisine" title="Ecuadorian cuisine">Ecuadorian cuisine</a> is diverse, varying with the altitude and associated agricultural conditions. Most regions in Ecuador follow the traditional three-course meal of soup, a course that includes rice and a protein, and then dessert and coffee to finish. </p>
      <p>In the highland region, various dishes of pork, chicken, beef, and <i>cuy</i> (guinea pig)<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> are popular and are served with a variety of grains (especially rice and <a href="/wiki/Mote_(food)" title="Mote (food)">mote</a>) or potatoes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In the coastal region, seafood is very popular, with fish, shrimp, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ceviche" title="Ceviche">ceviche</a></i> being key parts of the diet. Generally, ceviches are served with fried plantain (<a href="/wiki/Chifle" title="Chifle">chifles</a> or patacones), popcorn, or <a href="/wiki/Tostada_(tortilla)" title="Tostada (tortilla)">tostado</a>. <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">Plantain</a>- and peanut-based dishes are the basis of most coastal meals. Encocados (dishes that contain a coconut sauce) are also very popular. <i><a href="/wiki/Churrasco" title="Churrasco">Churrasco</a></i> is a staple food of the coastal region, especially <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>. <i>Arroz con menestra y carne asada</i> (rice with beans and grilled beef) is one of the traditional dishes of Guayaquil, as is <a href="/wiki/Tostones" title="Tostones">fried plantain</a>, which is often served with it. This region is a leading producer of <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa beans</a> (to make chocolate), shrimp, <a href="/wiki/Tilapia" title="Tilapia">tilapia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Passiflora_edulis" title="Passiflora edulis">passion fruit</a>, among other products.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In the Amazon region, a dietary staple is the <i>yuca</i>, elsewhere called <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>. Many fruits are available in this region, including <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyphostemma_juttae" title="Cyphostemma juttae">tree grapes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bactris_gasipaes" title="Bactris gasipaes">peach palms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jmontalvo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Jmontalvo.jpg/170px-Jmontalvo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Jmontalvo.jpg/255px-Jmontalvo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Jmontalvo.jpg/340px-Jmontalvo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="439" data-file-height="603"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jmontalvo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Juan_Montalvo" title="Juan Montalvo">Juan Montalvo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Early literature in colonial Ecuador, as in the rest of Spanish America, was influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Golden_Age" title="Spanish Golden Age">Spanish Golden Age</a>. One of the earliest examples is <a href="/wiki/Jacinto_Collahuazo" title="Jacinto Collahuazo">Jacinto Collahuazo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Boceto_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boceto-131">[131]</a></sup> an Amerindian chief of a northern village in today's Ibarra, born in the late 1600s. Despite the early repression and discrimination of the native people by the Spanish, Collahuazo learned to read and write in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Castilian</a>, but his work was written in <a href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a>. The use of <a href="/wiki/Quipu" title="Quipu">Quipu</a> was banned by the Spanish,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> and in order to preserve their work, many Inca poets had to resort to the use of the Latin alphabet to write in their native Quechua language. The history behind the Inca drama "Ollantay", the oldest literary piece in existence for any Amerindian language in America,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> shares some similarities with the work of Collahuazo. Collahuazo was imprisoned and all of his work burned. The existence of his literary work came to light many centuries later, when a crew of masons was restoring the walls of a colonial church in Quito and found a hidden manuscript. The salvaged fragment is a Spanish translation from Quechua of the "Elegy to the Dead of Atahualpa",<sup id="cite_ref-Boceto_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boceto-131">[131]</a></sup> a poem written by Collahuazo, which describes the sadness and impotence of the Inca people of having lost their king Atahualpa. </p>
      <p>Other early Ecuadorian writers include the Jesuits <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Aguirre" title="Juan Bautista Aguirre">Juan Bautista Aguirre</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Daule_Canton" title="Daule Canton">Daule</a> in 1725, and Father <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Velasco" title="Juan de Velasco">Juan de Velasco</a>, born in Riobamba in 1727. De Velasco wrote about the nations and chiefdoms that had existed in the <i>Kingdom of Quito</i> (today Ecuador) before the arrival of the Spanish. His historical accounts are nationalistic, featuring a romantic perspective of precolonial history. </p>
      <p>Famous authors from the late colonial and early republic period include <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Espejo" title="Eugenio Espejo">Eugenio Espejo</a>, a printer and main author of the first newspaper in Ecuadorian colonial times; <a href="/wiki/Jose_Joaquin_de_Olmedo" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Joaquin de Olmedo">Jose Joaquin de Olmedo</a> (born in Guayaquil), famous for his ode to <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> titled <i>Victoria de Junin</i>; <a href="/wiki/Juan_Montalvo" title="Juan Montalvo">Juan Montalvo</a>, a prominent essayist and novelist; <a href="/wiki/Juan_Leon_Mera" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Leon Mera">Juan Leon Mera</a>, famous for his work "Cumanda" or "Tragedy among Savages" and the Ecuadorian National Anthem; Juan A. Martinez with <i>A la Costa</i>; Dolores Veintimilla;<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> and others. </p>
      <p>Contemporary Ecuadorian writers include the novelist <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Enrique_Adoum" title="Jorge Enrique Adoum">Jorge Enrique Adoum</a>; the poet <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Carrera_Andrade" title="Jorge Carrera Andrade">Jorge Carrera Andrade</a>; the essayist <a href="/wiki/Benjam%C3%ADn_Carri%C3%B3n" title="Benjamín Carrión">Benjamín Carrión</a>; the poets Medardo Angel Silva, Jorge Carrera Andrade, and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Costales" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Costales">Luis Alberto Costales</a>; the novelist Enrique Gil Gilbert; the novelist <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Icaza" class="mw-redirect" title="Jorge Icaza">Jorge Icaza</a> (author of the novel <i>Huasipungo</i>, translated to many languages); the short story author Pablo Palacio; and the novelist Alicia Yanez Cossio. </p>
      <p>In spite of Ecuador's considerable mystique, it is rarely featured as a setting in contemporary western literature. One exception is "The Ecuadorian Deception," a murder mystery/thriller authored by American Bear Mills. In it, George d'Hout, a website designer from the United States is lured under false pretenses to Guayaquil. A corrupt American archaeologist is behind the plot, believing d'Hout holds the keys to locating a treasure hidden by a buccaneer ancestor. The story is based on a real pirate by the name of George d'Hout who terrorized Guayaquil in the 16th Century. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The best known art styles from Ecuador belonged to the <i><a href="/wiki/Escuela_Quite%C3%B1a" class="mw-redirect" title="Escuela Quiteña">Escuela Quiteña</a></i> (Quito School), which developed from the 16th to 18th centuries, examples of which are on display in various old churches in Quito. <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_painters" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecuadorian painters">Ecuadorian painters</a> include <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Kingman" title="Eduardo Kingman">Eduardo Kingman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oswaldo_Guayasam%C3%ADn" title="Oswaldo Guayasamín">Oswaldo Guayasamín</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Egas" title="Camilo Egas">Camilo Egas</a> from the Indiginist Movement; <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Rendon" title="Manuel Rendon">Manuel Rendon</a>, Jaime Zapata, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_T%C3%A1bara" title="Enrique Tábara">Enrique Tábara</a>, <a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_Villac%C3%ADs" title="Aníbal Villacís">Aníbal Villacís</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theo_Constant%C3%A9" title="Theo Constanté">Theo Constanté</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Molinari" title="Luis Molinari">Luis Molinari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Araceli_Gilbert" title="Araceli Gilbert">Araceli Gilbert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judith_Gutierrez" class="mw-redirect" title="Judith Gutierrez">Judith Gutierrez</a>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Arauz" title="Félix Arauz">Félix Arauz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Estuardo_Maldonado" title="Estuardo Maldonado">Estuardo Maldonado</a> from the Informalist Movement; <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Cobe%C3%B1a" title="Teddy Cobeña">Teddy Cobeña</a> from expressionism and figurative style<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and Luis Burgos Flor with his abstract, futuristic style. The Amerindian people of Tigua, Ecuador, are also world-renowned<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> for their <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Ecuador#Indigenous_art_of_Tigua" title="Culture of Ecuador">traditional paintings</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Ecuador" title="Sport in Ecuador">Sport in Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG/220px-Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG/330px-Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG/440px-Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Monumental_6.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Monumental_Isidro_Romero_Carbo" title="Estadio Monumental Isidro Romero Carbo">Estadio Monumental Isidro Romero Carbo</a> of Guayaquil
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The most popular <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Ecuador" title="Sport in Ecuador">sport in Ecuador</a>, as in most South American countries, is football. Its best known professional teams include; <a href="/wiki/Club_Sport_Emelec" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Sport Emelec">Emelec</a> from <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>, <a href="/wiki/LDU_Quito" class="mw-redirect" title="LDU Quito">Liga De Quito</a> from <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>; <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_S.C." title="Barcelona S.C.">Barcelona S.C.</a> from <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>, the most popular team in Ecuador, also the team with most local championships; <a href="/wiki/Sociedad_Deportivo_Quito" class="mw-redirect" title="Sociedad Deportivo Quito">Deportivo Quito</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_El_Nacional" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Deportivo El Nacional">El Nacional</a> from Quito; <a href="/wiki/Centro_Deportivo_Olmedo" class="mw-redirect" title="Centro Deportivo Olmedo">Olmedo</a> from <a href="/wiki/Riobamba" title="Riobamba">Riobamba</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Cuenca" class="mw-redirect" title="Club Deportivo Cuenca">Deportivo Cuenca</a> from Cuenca. Currently the most successful football team in Ecuador is LDU Quito, and it is the only Ecuadorian team that has won the <i><a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Copa_Sudamericana" title="Copa Sudamericana">Copa Sudamericana</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Recopa_Sudamericana" title="Recopa Sudamericana">Recopa Sudamericana</a></i>; they were also runners-up in the <a href="/wiki/2008_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2008 FIFA Club World Cup">2008 FIFA Club World Cup</a>. The matches of the <a href="/wiki/Ecuador_national_football_team" title="Ecuador national football team">Ecuadorian national team</a> are the most-watched sporting events in the country.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Ecuador has qualified for the final rounds of the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006</a>, &amp; the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a>. The 2002 FIFA World Cup qualifying campaign was considered a huge success for the country and its inhabitants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The unusually high elevation of the home stadium in Quito often affects the performance of visiting teams. Ecuador finished in 2nd place in the <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">CONMEBOL</a> qualifiers behind <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> and above the team that would become World Champions, <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>. In the 2006 FIFA World Cup, Ecuador finished ahead of <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">Costa Rica</a> finishing second behind <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> in Group A in the 2006 World Cup. They were defeated by <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> in the second round. </p>
      <p>Ecuador has won two medals in the Olympic Games, both gained by 20-km (12&nbsp;mi) racewalker <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_P%C3%A9rez" title="Jefferson Pérez">Jefferson Pérez</a>, who took gold in the <a href="/wiki/1996_Summer_Olympics" title="1996 Summer Olympics">1996</a> games and silver <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">12 years later</a>. Pérez also set a world best in the 2003 World Championships of 1:17:21 for the 20-km (12&nbsp;mi) distance.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Cycle_sport" title="Cycle sport">world class professional cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Carapaz" title="Richard Carapaz">Richard Carapaz</a> became the first Ecuadorian to win a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour_(cycling)" title="Grand Tour (cycling)">Grand Tour</a>. He won the <a href="/wiki/2019_Giro_d%27Italia" title="2019 Giro d'Italia">2019 Giro d'Italia</a><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Ecuador" title="Health in Ecuador">Health in Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg/220px-EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg/330px-EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg/440px-EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1678" data-file-height="1258"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:EC_Latacunga_Hospital_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>IESS Hospital in <a href="/wiki/Latacunga" title="Latacunga">Latacunga</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The current structure of the Ecuadorian public health care system dates back to 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The Ministry of the Public Health (Ministerio de Salud Pública del Ecuador) is the responsible entity of the regulation and creation of the public health policies and health care plans. The Minister of Public Health is appointed directly by the President of the Republic. The current minister, or Ecuadorian general surgeon, is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Margarita_Guevara&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Margarita Guevara (page does not exist)">Margarita Guevara</a>. </p>
      <p>The philosophy of the Ministry of Public Health is the social support and service to the most vulnerable population,<sup id="cite_ref-health_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health-142">[142]</a></sup> and its main plan of action lies around communitarian health and preventive medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-health_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health-142">[142]</a></sup> Many USA medical groups often visit regions away from the big cities to provide medical health to poor communities at their own expenses. It is known as medical missions some are Christian Organizations. </p>
      <p>The public healthcare system allows patients to be treated without an appointment in public general hospitals by general practitioners and specialists in the outpatient clinic (<i>Consulta Externa</i>) at no cost. This is done in the four basic specialties of pediatric, gynecology, clinic medicine, and surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-healths_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healths-143">[143]</a></sup> There are also public hospitals specialized to treat chronic diseases, target a particular group of the population, or provide better treatment in some medical specialties. Some examples in this group are the Gynecologic Hospitals, or Maternities, Children Hospitals, Geriatric Hospitals, and Oncology Institutes. </p>
      <p>Although well-equipped general hospitals are found in the major cities or capitals of provinces, there are basic hospitals in the smaller towns and <a href="/wiki/Canton_(country_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canton (country subdivision)">canton</a> cities for family care consultation and treatments in pediatrics, gynecology, clinical medicine, and surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-healths_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healths-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Community health care centers (Centros de Salud) are found inside metropolitan areas of cities and in rural areas. These are day hospitals that provide treatment to patients whose hospitalization is under 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-healths_143-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healths-143">[143]</a></sup> The doctors assigned to rural communities, where the Amerindian population can be substantial, have small clinics under their responsibility for the treatment of patients in the same fashion as the day hospitals in the major cities. The treatment in this case respects the culture of the community.<sup id="cite_ref-healths_143-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healths-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The public healthcare system should not be confused with the Ecuadorian Social Security healthcare service, which is dedicated to individuals with formal employment and who are affiliated obligatorily through their employers. Citizens with no formal employment may still contribute to the social security system voluntarily and have access to the medical services rendered by the social security system. The Ecuadorian Institute of Social Security (IESS) has several major hospitals and medical sub-centers under its administration across the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ecuador currently ranks 20, in most <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization_ranking_of_health_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="World Health Organization ranking of health systems">efficient health care countries</a>, compared to 111 back in the year 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Ecuadorians have a life expectancy of 77.1 years.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The infant mortality rate is 13 per 1,000 live births,<sup id="cite_ref-free_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-free-147">[147]</a></sup> a major improvement from approximately 76 in the early 1980s and 140 in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-148">[148]</a></sup> 23% of children under five are chronically malnourished.<sup id="cite_ref-free_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-free-147">[147]</a></sup> Population in some rural areas have no access to potable water, and its supply is provided by mean of water tankers. There are 686 malaria cases per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-fightingdiseases.org_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fightingdiseases.org-149">[149]</a></sup> Basic health care, including doctor's visits, basic surgeries, and basic medications, has been provided free since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-free_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-free-147">[147]</a></sup> However, some public hospitals are in poor condition and often lack necessary supplies to attend the high demand of patients. Private hospitals and clinics are well equipped but still expensive for the majority of the population. </p>
      <p>Between 2008 and 2016, new public hospitals have been built, the number of civil servants has increased significantly and salaries have been increased. In 2008, the government introduced universal and compulsory social security coverage. In 2015, corruption remains a problem. Overbilling is recorded in 20% of public establishments and in 80% of private establishments.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rectorado_noche.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Rectorado_noche.jpg/200px-Rectorado_noche.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Rectorado_noche.jpg/300px-Rectorado_noche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Rectorado_noche.jpg/400px-Rectorado_noche.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="872"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rectorado_noche.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rectorate building of the <a href="/wiki/Escuela_Superior_Politecnica_del_Litoral" title="Escuela Superior Politecnica del Litoral">Higher Polytechnic School of the Litoral</a> of Guayaquil
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Ecuador" title="Education in Ecuador">Education in Ecuador</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Quito_Observatory_04.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Quito_Observatory_04.JPG/200px-Quito_Observatory_04.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Quito_Observatory_04.JPG/300px-Quito_Observatory_04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Quito_Observatory_04.JPG/400px-Quito_Observatory_04.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Quito_Observatory_04.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The oldest observatory in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Quito_Astronomical_Observatory" title="Quito Astronomical Observatory">Quito Astronomical Observatory</a>, founded in 1873 and located in <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, Ecuador. The Quito Astronomical Observatory is managed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_School" class="mw-redirect" title="National Polytechnic School">National Polytechnic School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Ecuadorian Constitution requires that all children attend school until they achieve a "basic level of education", which is estimated at nine school years.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-152">[152]</a></sup> In 1996, the net primary enrollment rate was 96.9%, and 71.8% of children stayed in school until the fifth grade / age 10.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-152">[152]</a></sup> The cost of primary and secondary education is borne by the government, but families often face significant additional expenses such as fees and transportation costs.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-152">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Provision of public schools falls far below the levels needed, and class sizes are often very large, and families of limited means often find it necessary to pay for education.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> In rural areas, only 10% of the children go on to high school.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The Ministry of Education states that the mean number of years completed is 6.7.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg/170px-Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg/255px-Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg/340px-Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colegio_Maldonado_Riobamba.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maldonado High School of <a href="/wiki/Riobamba" title="Riobamba">Riobamba</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador has 61 universities, many of which still confer <a href="/wiki/Terminal_degree" title="Terminal degree">terminal degrees</a> according to the traditional Spanish education system,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> honoring a long tradition of having some of the oldest universities in the Americas: University of San Fulgencio, founded in 1586 by the Augustines; San Gregorio Magno University, founded in 1651 by the Jesuits; and University of Santo Tomás of Aquino, founded in 1681 by the Dominican order. </p>
      <p>Among the traditional conferred terminal degrees can be noted the doctorate for medicine and law schools or engineering, physics, chemistry, or mathematics for polytechnic or technology institutes. These terminal degrees, as in the case of the PhD in other countries, were the main requirement for an individual to be accepted in academia as a professor or researcher. In the professional realm, a terminal degree granted by an accredited institution automatically provides a professional license to the individual. </p>
      <p>However, in 2004, the National Council of Higher Education (CONESUP), started the reorganization of all the degree-granting schemes of the accredited universities in order to pair them with foreign counterparts. The new structure of some careers caused the dropping of subjects, credits, or even the name of the previously conferred diplomas. The terminal degree in law, previously known as JD <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">Juris Doctor</a> (Doctor en Jurisprudencia) was replaced by the one of <i>abogado</i> (attorney) with the exception of the modification of the number of credits to equate it to an undergraduate degree. In the same fashion for medical school, the required time of education was considerably reduced from nine years (the minimum needed to obtain the title of MD in Medicine and Surgery) to almost five, with the provision that the diploma is not terminal anymore, and it is given with the title of <i>médico</i> (medic). Therefore, an MD or PhD in medicine is only to be obtained overseas until the universities adjust themselves to granting schemes and curriculum as in foreign counterparts. Nonetheless, a "médico" can start a career as family practitioner or general medicine physician. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg/200px-SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg/300px-SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg/400px-SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SageoEG_-_Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Municipal_de_Guayaquil" title="Biblioteca Municipal de Guayaquil">Municipal Library of Guayaquil</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>This new reorganization, although very ambitious, lacked the proper path to the homologation of diplomas for highly educated professionals graduated in the country or even for the ones graduated in foreign institutions. One of the points of conflict was the imposition of obtaining foreign degrees to current academicians. As today, a master's degree is a requirement to keep an academic position and at least a foreign PhD to attain or retain the status of <i>rector</i> (president of a university) or <i>décano</i> (dean). For Ecuadorian researchers and many academicians trained in the country, these regulations sounded illogical, disappointing, and unlawful since it appeared a question of a title name conflict rather than specialization or science advancement. </p>
      <p>A debate to modify this and other reforms, especially the one which granted control of the Higher Education System by the government, was practically passed with consensus by the multi-partisan National Assembly on August 4, 2010, but vetoed by President <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Correa" title="Rafael Correa">Rafael Correa</a>, who wanted to keep the law strictly as it was originally redacted by his political party and SENPLADES (National Secretary of Planning and Development). Due to this change, there are many highly educated professionals and academicians under the old structure but estimated that only 87% of the faculty in public universities have already obtained a master's degree, and fewer than 5% have a PhD (although many of them already have Ecuadorian-granted doctorate degrees). </p>
      <p>About 300 institutes of higher education offer two to three years of post-secondary vocational or technical training. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sciences_and_research">Sciences and research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Sciences and research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg/220px-NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg/330px-NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg/440px-NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NEE-01-PEGASO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_Civilian_Space_Agency" title="Ecuadorian Civilian Space Agency">EXA</a>'s first satellite, <a href="/wiki/NEE-01_Pegasus" class="mw-redirect" title="NEE-01 Pegasus">NEE-01 Pegasus</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ecuador is currently placed in 96th position of innovation in technology.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> The most notable icons in Ecuadorian sciences are the mathematician and cartographer <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Vicente_Maldonado" title="Pedro Vicente Maldonado">Pedro Vicente Maldonado</a>, born in Riobamba in 1707, and the printer, independence precursor, and medical pioneer <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Espejo" title="Eugenio Espejo">Eugenio Espejo</a>, born in 1747 in Quito. Among other notable Ecuadorian scientists and engineers are Lieutenant Jose Rodriguez Labandera,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> a pioneer who built the first <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a> in Latin America in 1837; <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinaldo_Espinosa_Aguilar" class="extiw" title="es:Reinaldo Espinosa Aguilar">Reinaldo Espinosa Aguilar</a> (1898–1950), a botanist and biologist of Andean flora; and <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Aurelio_Due%C3%B1as" class="extiw" title="es:José Aurelio Dueñas">José Aurelio Dueñas</a> (1880–1961), a chemist and inventor of a method of textile serigraphy. </p>
      <p>The major areas of scientific research in Ecuador have been in the medical fields, tropical and infectious diseases treatments, agricultural engineering, pharmaceutical research, and bioengineering. Being a small country and a consumer of foreign technology, Ecuador has favored research supported by entrepreneurship in information technology. The antivirus program <i>Checkprogram</i>, banking protection system <i>MdLock</i>, and Core Banking Software <i>Cobis</i> are products of Ecuadorian development.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The scientific production in hard sciences has been limited due to lack of funding but focused around physics, statistics, and partial differential equations in mathematics.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the case of engineering fields, the majority of scientific production comes from the top three polytechnic institutions: Escuela Superior Politécnica del Litoral - <i><a href="/wiki/Escuela_Superior_Politecnica_del_Litoral" title="Escuela Superior Politecnica del Litoral">ESPOL</a></i>, Universidad de Las Fuerzas Armadas - <i><a href="/wiki/ESPE" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPE">ESPE</a></i>, and Escuela Politécnica Nacional <i><a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_School" class="mw-redirect" title="National Polytechnic School">EPN</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Research_and_Technology_Development_in_Ecuador" title="Center for Research and Technology Development in Ecuador">Center for Research and Technology Development in Ecuador</a> is an autonomous center for research and technology development funded by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senecyt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Senecyt (page does not exist)">Senecyt</a>. </p>
      <p>However, according to <a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a>, the multidisciplinary scientific journal the top 10 institutions that carry the most outstanding scientific contributions are: Yachay Tech University (<a href="/wiki/Yachay_University" title="Yachay University"><i>Yachay Tech</i></a>), Escuela Politécnica Nacional (<i><a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_School" class="mw-redirect" title="National Polytechnic School">EPN</a>)</i>, and Universidad San Francisco de Quito <i>(<a href="/wiki/Universidad_San_Francisco_de_Quito" title="Universidad San Francisco de Quito">USFQ</a>).</i><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_Index_-_Top_10_institutions_from_Ecuador">Nature Index - Top 10 institutions from Ecuador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Nature Index - Top 10 institutions from Ecuador">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <table class="wikitable">

         <td>1 </td> 
         <td>0.11 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>EPN is known for research and education in the <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">applied science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_physics" title="Atmospheric physics">atmospheric physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physical_sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Physical sciences">physical sciences</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Geophysics" title="Geophysics">Geophysics</a> Institute<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> monitors over the country's <a href="/wiki/Volcanoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanoes">volcanoes</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Andes_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Andes Mountains">Andes Mountains</a> of Ecuador and in the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos Islands</a>, all of which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a>. EPN adopted the <a href="/wiki/History_of_European_research_universities" class="mw-redirect" title="History of European research universities">polytechnic university model</a> that stresses laboratory instruction in applied science and engineering. </p>
      <p>The oldest observatory in South America is the <a href="/wiki/Quito_Astronomical_Observatory" title="Quito Astronomical Observatory">Quito Astronomical Observatory</a> and is located in Quito, Ecuador. The Quito Astronomical Observatory, which gives the global community of a Virtual Telescope System that is connected via the Internet and allows the world to watch by streaming, is managed by EPN. </p>
      <p>Contemporary Ecuadorian scientists who have been recognized by international institutions are Eugenia del Pino (born 1945), the first Ecuadorian to be elected to the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="National Academy of Science">National Academy of Science</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Villavicencio" title="Arturo Villavicencio">Arturo Villavicencio</a>, who was part of the working group of the IPCC, which shared the <a href="/wiki/2007_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2007 Nobel Peace Prize">2007 Nobel Peace Prize</a> with <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> for their dissemination of the effects of climate change. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Performance_Computing">High Performance Computing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: High Performance Computing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Ecuadorian institutions compute extensive information using supercomputers such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quinde_I_supercomputer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Quinde I supercomputer (page does not exist)">Quinde I</a>, the most powerful of that country performing 232 <a href="/wiki/FLOPS" title="FLOPS">TeraFLOPS</a>. </p>
      <p>Institutions that have <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">High Performance Computing</a> centers:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-161">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_School_(Ecuador)" title="National Polytechnic School (Ecuador)">National Polytechnic School</a> <i>(EPN)</i></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_University_-_ESPE" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed Forces University - ESPE">Armed Forces University</a> <i>(ESPE)</i></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Universidad_San_Francisco_de_Quito" title="Universidad San Francisco de Quito">Universidad San Francisco de Quito</a> <i>(USFQ)</i></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Universidad_T%C3%A9cnica_Particular_de_Loja" title="Universidad Técnica Particular de Loja">Universidad Técnica Particular de Loja</a> <i>(UTPL)</i></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Cuenca" title="University of Cuenca">University of Cuenca</a><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Yachay_University" title="Yachay University">Yachay Tech University</a> <i>(YT)</i></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Currently, the politics of research and investigation are managed by the National Secretary of Higher Education, Science, and Technology (<i>Senescyt</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecuador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
